<div id="review_750439814" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/750439814" />
    <a title="Louise" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9627459-louise"><img alt="Louise" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1372421756p2/9627459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/750439814?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louise" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louise" href="/user/show/9627459-louise">Louise</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9627459-louise?shelf=book-hangover">book-hangover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9627459-louise?shelf=soul-shattering">soul-shattering</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer750439814" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16147584300772356640"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>In a dream, in a fairy tale, nothing has to be explained, everything happens of its own accord.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383742242ra/6651121.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Have you ever wonder, <b>do all Fairy tales have a happy ending?</b><br/>What if if it doesn't but what if it doesn't matter.<br/><br/>This is one of them books I can't get over with, it’s still there lingering from my memory, like it was real, like it IS real and I can hardly shake it. The worse of it all was I can't properly eat and sleep after finishing this book.<br/><br/><b>This is a story of innocence</b><br/><i>
  <blockquote>Somebody was ru</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText16147584300772356640" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>In a dream, in a fairy tale, nothing has to be explained, everything happens of its own accord.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1383742242ra/6651121.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Have you ever wonder, <b>do all Fairy tales have a happy ending?</b><br>What if if it doesn't but what if it doesn't matter.<br><br>This is one of them books I can't get over with, it’s still there lingering from my memory, like it was real, like it IS real and I can hardly shake it. The worse of it all was I can't properly eat and sleep after finishing this book.<br><br><b>This is a story of innocence</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>Somebody was running toward him, somebody who had been waiting in the shadows. Somebody small in a worn, pink down jacket. They flew toward each other, the small and tall figures, with arms outstretched—their feet didn’t seem to touch the ground—they met in the middle. The tall figure lifted up the small one, spun her around through the winter air, once, twice, three times in a whirl of light, childish laughter.</blockquote>
</i><br><b>Love</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>
<br> …suddenly, Abel pulled her into the doorway beside the shop window,…His lips were as cold as snow, but beyond the lips lay the warmth of a fairy-tale sun.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>Magic</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>The rainbows began to swirl into each other, as if they were threads themselves. They danced and spun around; they formed spirals and knots up there, in the clear, cold winter air…</blockquote>
</i><br><b>Danger</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>There is blood everywhere… the tiles are cold and white as snow, and it is winter.<br>It will be winter forever.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>Friendship</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>...in summer, I want to swim with you, right here. We’ll lie in the water just like this, only the sky will be a different color then. And the water will be warm and blue, and the sailors will pass us on their way out to the island of Rügen.”<br>“And we’ll eat loads of ice cream,” Micha added.<br>“Definitely.” Abel rolled onto his stomach. “And then we’ll lounge around on the beach all lazy,<br>and we’ll build sandcastles …”<br>“With sea grass for decoration and pinecones for inhabitants,” Anna said.</blockquote>
</i><br><br><br><b>Heartbreak</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>“...we can do everything, Abel … get anywhere … together …”<br>He smiled. “Everything?” he said. “Together. With me? Anna Leemann, you don’t even know me.”<br> “Go away, princess. Leave your outlaw alone. You won’t … you won’t change him.”<br>
</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>Forgiveness</b><br><i>
  <blockquote>“So let’s not forgive,” she whispered. “Nor forget. The night will remain there. Behind us.”<br>“But still you’re here.”<br>“But still I’m here.”</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>Hope</b> <br><i>
  <blockquote> ‘If we lose each other? Where will we find each other again?’<br>“‘We’ll meet wherever spring is,’</blockquote>
</i><br><br><b>Sacrifice</b><br><br><b>
  <i>
    <blockquote>In love, there is no criticism. In love, there is no rationality.<br>
</blockquote>
  </i>
</b><br>----------------------------------------------------------------------------<br><b>green military parka</b><br><br>Abel might be one those characters I just want to reach out, I want to jump inside the book and hug him. He is such a broken young man and so sweet and caring to his sister. He'll protect her from all dangers and that no one we'll part them both. He's a closed off hero, and that's made him more intriguing and secretive but what I love about him was his storytelling. He'd crafted all this scenarios the same as their real life and I was so glued on what will happen next. I hate him on some part though I can't help but love him on other parts too. I'm still thinking about him after I finished this book... It was insane!<br><br><b>five tiny freckles</b><br>Ana oh Ana, this girl omg her curiosity over the taste of something different in life got her in a roller coaster of events. How she had fit herself in the world of Abel and Micha was something I would call "magical" and unexpected yet she fits perfectly well for them and I'm so glad she became a part of their lives. I hate her wild decisions its gets her into trouble but I do know she was deciding from her heart and not her mind, she might be reckless in doing so but her love for Abel was beyond all reasons. It was the staggering truth that she will still love him "against all odds". <br><br><b>pink down jacket</b><br>Micha, my sweet sweet little girl, she's a bucket of love, joy, innocence and courage. She's a wise girl and she's the light in the story. For me, she's the one who made Abel and Anna closer together.<br><br><b>color of poppies or is it anemones</b><br>the fairytale that seemingly coated with innocence while it actually drench in malice was as intriguing as the reality in the story. The subtle tone of how the fairytale was told to the suspenseful part of of their reality that is yet to be solve was beautifully written but no matter how poetical it was the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[gory <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> scenes( watch out for that) was difficult to take because it was written in detailed O_O<br> <br><b>White noise</b><br>You know the thing you hear when there's no reception in the radio, a white noise. I want that right now and forget all the bad stuff that happened in the book and focus the the beautiful fairytale instead and the skating part too which was my favorite scene and all the stolen kisses *sigh* <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1388288072i/7788458.jpg" width="370" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*a little reminder to the future readers of this book:<br><b>Guard your heart...it might shatter into a thousand pieces.</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1422151960i/13463436._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_553187914" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/553187914" />
    <a title="Mags~CVAddikt~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5715052-mags-cvaddikt"><img alt="Mags~CVAddikt~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483979478p2/5715052.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/553187914?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mags~CVAddikt~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mags~CVAddikt~" href="/user/show/5715052-mags-cvaddikt">Mags~CVAddikt~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13416698-the-storyteller">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Mags~CVAddikt~ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/5565340-i">I</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=big-fat-tears">big-fat-tears</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=throw-it-in-the-freezer">throw-it-in-the-freezer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=the-pain-so-much-pain">the-pain-so-much-pain</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=drama-total">drama-total</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=dark-oscuro-donker-sombre">dark-oscuro-donker-sombre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=addictive-like-chocolate">addictive-like-chocolate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=favorites-2013">favorites-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=5-stars-2013">5-stars-2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5715052-mags-cvaddikt?shelf=new-adult-contemporary-fiction">new-adult-contemporary-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer553187914" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13403652208124462579"><blockquote>
  <i> “The wolf didn’t reply. ‘You’re shivering,’ he said. ‘Do you believe that you could spin a thread of my blood? To make clothes from?’”</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Maybe that’s not the most dramatic-heart-wrenching quote of the book, but in my opinion, this quote holds the essence of the story, of Abel. <br/><br/>If you are looking for a New Adult book with the typical NA-Formula of<br/>“HOT GUY + HOT GIRL + TRAGIC PAST + SMEXY TIME + HEALING OF A BROKEN HEARTH” then go read something else. <br/><br/>If you can stomach raw cruel realistic ficti</span>
  <span id="freeText13403652208124462579" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i> “The wolf didn’t reply. ‘You’re shivering,’ he said. ‘Do you believe that you could spin a thread of my blood? To make clothes from?’”</i>
</blockquote><br><br>Maybe that’s not the most dramatic-heart-wrenching quote of the book, but in my opinion, this quote holds the essence of the story, of Abel. <br><br>If you are looking for a New Adult book with the typical NA-Formula of<br>“HOT GUY + HOT GIRL + TRAGIC PAST + SMEXY TIME + HEALING OF A BROKEN HEARTH” then go read something else. <br><br>If you can stomach raw cruel realistic fiction, then go ahead and read this book. Ohh but don’t get me wrong, there is a <s>beautiful</s> <em>bittersweet</em> story behind, this book is about <strong>LOVE, SACRIFICE</strong> and the <strong>INJUSTICE</strong> in life. <br><br>One day, Anna found a doll, hidden at school, and Abel claimed it belonged to his little sister Micha. Anna was intrigued; she followed him, met his sister, and became involved in their lives. Abel’s mother disappeared, and he was desperate to keep Micha by his side, because he was underage. Anna helped him take care of Micha.<br><br><b>Anna</b><br><br>At first, I disliked her a bit. Anna is a girl that has had a comfortable life, but she also feels trapped by so much <em>perfection</em>.<br><br><i>“Who was she? A girl inside a bubble. The daughter of Magnus and Linda Leemann, from a nice district of Griefswald, from a house of blue air. High school student in her last year, musician, English au pair to be. Gitta’s squeaky-clean little lamb. No. She was someone who didn’t know yet who she was or would be.”</i><br><br>Maybe is that motherly instinct, we girls have, to fix something broken that made Anna get involved with Abel and Micha, maybe it was the amazing talent Abel had for telling beautiful stories based in an ugly reality, or maybe it was the need of adventure … what ever the reason was, Anna took an important role in the story, in their lives, and she was so involved in the swirl of fire that was Abel and Micha’s lives that it sucked her up completely, it consumed her ... and she got burned … <br><br><br><b>Abel</b><br><br>Oh boy … where do I start? How can I explain a character that … argh!!! He’s a protective brother, a drug dealer, an abused child, a selfless person, a great storyteller, a talented writer …. And he’s also so messed up that he makes bad choices, he has all that rage inside, he’s self-destructive, but also loyal, he’s violent, and tender, angry and intimidating, he’s afraid and he has hope and he had to grow up quickly and … and … and he’s blind to the other options around him, he’s vindictive … and … Just trying to figure him out drains me emotionally. <br><br>And that’s the thing with this book, it is a roller coaster of emotions and it challenged my moral and ethical principles, I was so immersed in the story that I found myself rooting for “unreasonable Anna”, I wanted her to make a bad choice, I was <em>justifying</em> Abel’s actions … and … NO … just … <strong>NO</strong> … as he said:<br><blockquote>
<br><i>”There is a reason for what happened. I can’t be forgiven so I am not asking you for forgiveness. We lost each other, and we will never find each other again.”</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412209ra/810555.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b>Yeah!! That's what I say about the boat house scene!!!!</b><br><br><br>By the end of the book, I was a mess … I was trying to cope and process and order my thoughts … this book was recommended to my by a friend, when she finished, she called me and said something like “I just finished ‘The Storyteller’ and I need to go out, let’s go for coffee because … I need to process this” ….. not her exact words, but you get the idea. Well … sadly I couldn’t go for coffee with her, but after I finished reading … I called her and told her “I get it, I do …. WHY DID YOU MAKE ME READ THIS DRAMATIC BOOK!!?? WHAT DID I EVER DO TO YOU!!?? THE PAIN!! SO MUCH PAIN!!” <br><br>Really, my reaction at the end was something like …<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380412209ra/810556.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/451892.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380412209i/810557.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Now you are probably asking yourself ... should I read this??? <br><b>YES!!! READ IT!!!! </b><br>.<br>.<br>.<br>I don't want to suffer alone ... <br><br><br><br><br>Free time = new project ... check out this review in my blog...<br><a href="http://1000addictions.wordpress.com/2013/07/05/the-storyteller/" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364633i/716394._SX540_.png" width="350" height="110" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13403652208124462579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2419236763" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2419236763" />
    <a title="Literatures Movies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66216992-literatures-movies"><img alt="Literatures Movies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1522073764p2/66216992.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2419236763?book_show_action=true">Feb 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Literatures Movies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Literatures Movies" href="/user/show/66216992-literatures-movies">Literatures Movies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66216992-literatures-movies?shelf=dnf">dnf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2419236763" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16406473658991226026"><br/>Yes, ladies and gentlemen.<br/><br/>As we all have started to guess by now, if a book takes longer than a few days for me to finish, there's a high chance that it's gonna turn into a DNF for me. <br/><br/>And <i>lo and behold</i>, we have a fucking DNF. <br/><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533021067ra/26054200.gif' width='450' height='250' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Honestly, maybe this is my final call to steer off and clear of YA. Cause damn baby, I tried. I tried, and tried, and fucking tried again, and again, and a-fucking-gain. But YA is just not for me anymore I'm afraid. Other than a very few selected authors, that is. <br/><br/>Regardin</span>
  <span id="freeText16406473658991226026" style="display:none"><br>Yes, ladies and gentlemen.<br><br>As we all have started to guess by now, if a book takes longer than a few days for me to finish, there's a high chance that it's gonna turn into a DNF for me. <br><br>And <i>lo and behold</i>, we have a fucking DNF. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1533021067ra/26054200.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, maybe this is my final call to steer off and clear of YA. Cause damn baby, I tried. I tried, and tried, and fucking tried again, and again, and a-fucking-gain. But YA is just not for me anymore I'm afraid. Other than a very few selected authors, that is. <br><br>Regarding The Storyteller, I don't have anything good to say about it, to be quite honest with you.<br><br>The characters –– Abel and (fuck I already forgot her name) Anna –– was boring as fuck all. It was literally like reading two bricks trying to communicate. One was a sheltered brick, one was a broken brick with hard edges. Ya know, the normal good girl bad boy trope. <br><br>Which is fine. We shall give it the benefit of the doubt, cause why not.<br><br>And then we get to know our beloved bricks. And <b>guess what ? </b><br><br><b>THEY HAVE THE PERSONALITY OF BRICKS </b><br><br>Reading how to cook eggs would be more exciting and entertaining to me than this book. <br><br>They were supposed to be "in love" and "hot for each other". This book was listed under romance, but unless we're talking about how Anna's stalker was borderline obsessive with her (which isn't the main story at all), I don't see anything romantic about this story. <br><br>Another thing is the writing. Like, <i>I get it</i>. You want this book to be pleasing. So you set up to write all the long ass proses that was supposed to be "beautiful" and whatnot. But damn bitch, this shit is anything but. <br><br>It's so heavy with so much unneeded words and pretty proses and "supposed sexual tension" that I grew tired and sleepy after reading 2 chapters. <br><br>No, like literally. I have to fucking nap after reading a few chapters. <b>That's how fucking draining this book was</b>.<br><br>I forced myself to read 41% of it, and honestly, after reaching 41%, I can't say I learned anything new about the plot nor the characters. Other than the fact that our main female character Anna is tired of her pretty, sheltered, comfy life and wants to flirt with danger that is packaged in a broody yet sexy brick called Abel. <br><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1519298048ra/25103093.gif" width="450" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As for all the sad parts, or the traumatic parts, or whatever parts that were to come that managed to earn this book such high ratings, sorry to disappoint folks, but I didn't –– nor did I want to –– stay long enough to find out.<br><br>Now if you'd excuse me, I'm off to find some other good books that didn't take me fucking weeks to get through. <br><br><br><br><b>Blog : <a href="http://literaturesandmovies.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Me, in all of my writing glory</a><br><br>Youtube : <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UCeEAFz7timmDVbph_Mgox6Q" rel="nofollow noopener">And sometimes I talk about random shits here </a><br><br>IG : <a href="http://instagram.com/caterpillarbuddies/" rel="nofollow noopener">and IG account where I mostly use it to stalk pretty humans</a></b></span>
  <a data-text-id="16406473658991226026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/292336678?book_show_action=true">Mar 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE!</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253942-kajal-nehra?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer292336678" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7754936246256857338"><b>Just a tiny little pain,<br/>Three days of heavy rain,<br/>Three days of sunlight,<br/>Everything will be all right.<br/>Just a tiny little pain...</b><br/><br/><b>5 STARS!!!</b> Hell, 10 stars!<br/><br/>OH MY GOSH... I'm actually in a state of shock right now. Each time that scene (please do not click on the spoiler until you've read the book or else you'll loathe me FOREVER!!!) <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[when Abel calls Anna's name, smiles and puts the gun's barrel in his mouth, doesn't even hesitate for a second... and its done. He's gone. Forever. No mo</span></span>
  <span id="freeText7754936246256857338" style="display:none"><b>Just a tiny little pain,<br>Three days of heavy rain,<br>Three days of sunlight,<br>Everything will be all right.<br>Just a tiny little pain...</b><br><br><b>5 STARS!!!</b> Hell, 10 stars!<br><br>OH MY GOSH... I'm actually in a state of shock right now. Each time that scene (please do not click on the spoiler until you've read the book or else you'll loathe me FOREVER!!!) <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[when Abel calls Anna's name, smiles and puts the gun's barrel in his mouth, doesn't even hesitate for a second... and its done. He's gone. Forever. No more... (Fuck! I'm crying all over again!) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>Someone will never turn eighteen. All the plans someone had of a summer - of the day they'll be able to make something come true for which they'd waited SO LONG - will never be fulfilled.<br><br>Just one shot and its over. God, I know I'm being so effing hollow here, but I <i>feel</i> hollow dammit! Just think about it that way, and you'll be soon drowning in your own tears.<br><br><i>The Storyteller</i> is a very <b>realistic</b> and <b>heart-wrenching</b> read, which will constrict your throat not just once but many times through it. You'll be begging for the oxygen which will refuse to come to you.<br><br>I don't even have words to say anything about it, so I'm just going to leave it here. Maybe later on, when I'm outta my shock I'll edit this and make the review sound more plausible, but for now this is all I can give you. Just one thing I'd like to tell you ALL: <b>Read</b> <i>The Storyteller</i>! Read it. Or else you'll forever be sorry for letting something as exceptional as this pass by.<br><br>The anemones:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380372046i/725221.jpg" width="250" height="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <span id="freeText13096981066469601909" style="display:none"><b>A MILLION STARS... I LOVED IT.. I LIVED IT.. IT KILLED ME.. <br><br>A MASTERPIECE.. ALL OF IT.. I LOVED IT.. She saw him lying there, saw the blood in which he lay, so incomprehensibly red, light red—big, burst droplets of blood the color of poppies. A sea of blood, a red endless sea, crimson waves, carmine froth, splashing color … Micha was kneeling next to his legs and had laid her arms and her head on his knees, where there was no blood. And she was singing, very, very softly.<br><br>Just a tiny little pain,<br>Three days of heavy rain,<br>Three days of sunlight,<br>Everything will be all right.<br>Just a tiny little pain horrible things, but i couldn't get my self to hate him, i felt sorry for him, i even loved a part of him, the part that loved his sister unconditionally, the big brother that took care and held the burden of a six years old.. i love <i>that</i> Abel..<br><br><i>“I am not staying with the murderer," she said, her words muffled by his jacket. "I am not staying with the victim Abel Tannatek or the culprit Abel Tannatek. I am staying with the storyteller.” <br></i><br><br>Those are exactly my thoughts, and u can't ignore the fact that he is a corrupted kid, abused at the age of 10 for 2 years..<br>he was terrified that his sister might live what he had to live through, but then when he knew that his sister would be fine, he could finally rest, and found a way out...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380436052ra/881185.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Abel,, i wish he didn't do that, i wish he could have had a better life.. <br><br>Some lines i loved:<br><br><i>“Everybody knew everything now. Or did everybody know nothing? Nobody knew anything... There are fewer answers in the world than questions, and if you ask me now why that is so, I must tell you that there is no answer to that question.” <br></i><br><br><i>“There was the place where all the shouted words fall into the water. They’re too weak to make it from shore to shore. I saw the words underwater, millions of them; they’re lying there on the bottom of the sea, a whole load of wrecked sentences, sentences that never reached their destination, questions from one side and answers from the other…” <br></i><br><br>the end.. sorry for the long review :D<br><br>~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~~<br><br>I thank u Zemira, love, thanx for recommending and telling me to be patient.. i love this book.. thank u &lt;3<br></span>

<div id="review_230037606" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/230037606" />
    <a title="Fathima" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5799807-fathima"><img alt="Fathima" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605105757p2/5799807.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/230037606?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Fathima" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Fathima" href="/user/show/5799807-fathima">Fathima</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13416698-the-storyteller">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer230037606" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4850296840721743635"><b> Just a tiny little pain,<br/> Three days of heavy rain,<br/> Three days of sunlight, <br/> Everything will be alright .<br/> Just a tiny little pain ..... </b><br/> <br/>An hour and a half has passed , and the only sensible thing that i've done in that past hour is cry . Cry , because that seemed the only way to get rid of the pain . Pain , that this soul stiring , questioning your beliefs on love and forgiveness kind of feel this book leaves you with . I would be lying if i said that i've heard or read this kind of a story bef</span>
  <span id="freeText4850296840721743635" style="display:none"><b> Just a tiny little pain,<br /> Three days of heavy rain,<br /> Three days of sunlight, <br /> Everything will be alright .<br /> Just a tiny little pain ..... </b><br /> <br />An hour and a half has passed , and the only sensible thing that i've done in that past hour is cry . Cry , because that seemed the only way to get rid of the pain . Pain , that this soul stiring , questioning your beliefs on love and forgiveness kind of feel this book leaves you with . I would be lying if i said that i've heard or read this kind of a story before , and i would also be lying if i told that i have cried this way for too long before . Never before have i felt an emotion so strong , so over whelming that i know i could move a mountain or control the waves of the ocean with it . The storyteller is a book with so many riled up different kinds of emotions , that i felt that its really upto the reader to either submerge oneself in the vast depthness of this book or just skim the surface . Either way it is impossible to walk away unscathed . A thorn of pain , a sprinkle of laughter , a touch of innocence , an hint of unspoken love , a trickle of tear , a spark of anger , its bound to touch you , bound to make you feel good or bad depending on the aura around the story . <br /><br />Cover speak : Absolutely and whole heartedly love this cover . For me its meaning were simple , the rose there being the sign/symbol of love and hope . But one must not forget that along with the roses comes its thorns . Along with love comes its share of pain and heatbreaks . And sometimes hope crumbles too , giving way to agony and despair . The droplets of blood around are just that . One could also say that it symbolises 'Tainted love ' . Why do i call it tainted ? Well you will just have to read the story and find out . <br /><br />Honestly , the blurb of this book already talks about what this book and its story line and everything is ... but , in no freaking ways does it prepare you for what you are about to get into once you actually start reading it . It basically gives you moments and memories , that tends to linger with you even after you've long finished reading this masterpiece . <br /><br />When an author manages to bring out the most complexes of human nature by spinning a tale of loss , love , pain and sacrifice then i believe that author has managed to win and conquer the hearts of all those who've read their work . And Antonia Michaelis is one such author . She apeaks of the human nature , the human trait to protect someone near and dear more than protecting ones own life , to love someone deeply without conditions , to follow dreams to secure someone else's future more than yours , to kill or be killed without hesitation and regrets . <br />All these above mentioned points are just a part of this amazing story . <br />Another very inspiring point of this book was Abels story telling technique . How easily it could be called a work of imagination yet its full of reality and truth . Oh my i'm totally in love with the characters and this book ... Even now as i sit here and type out this review , i cant help but get all teary eyed .. * Sobs * <br /><br /><u> My playlist for this book </u> :<br />1) Massive Attack - Paradise Circus . ( Overview of the entire book ) <br />2) Florence and the Machine - Blinding . ( When Micah calls up Anna , telling her Abel's in trouble and Anna runs out to help them )<br />3) Deftones - Minerva ( Abel's song ) <br />4) Cider Sky - Northern Lights ( Abel and Anna's intimate moments ) <br />5) Massive Attack - Risingson ( In most of the scenes at the club ) <br />6) Paper Route - Dancing on our Graves ( Abels song for Anna after their night at the boathouse )<br />7) Sade - King of Sorrow ( Anna's song for Abel ) <br />8) Kings of leon - Closer<br />9) Florence and the Machine - Cosmic love <br />10) Civil Wars - Poison and wine ( For the end )<br /><br />I would seriously recommend this book to everyone !! This was such a fabulous read , soooo glad i read it !! A story of life , love , death and everything in between !! </span>
  <a data-text-id="4850296840721743635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_422502774" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/422502774" />
    <a title="Ails" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12873266-ails"><img alt="Ails" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351577137p2/12873266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/422502774?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ails" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ails" href="/user/show/12873266-ails">Ails</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=thriller">thriller</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12873266-ails?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422502774" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10229043585426932063">5 STARS. <i>(EDIT: With more details)</i><br/><br/>There are two kinds of a good book: those that you enjoy but will soon forget, and those that will linger in your memory forever. "The Storyteller" is the latter.<br/><br/><i>It's unlike anything you have ever read. Trust me.</i><br/><br/>This book is brilliantly, beautifully written by Antonia Michaelis. I'm completely mesmerized by her words and her ability to interweave magic and realism in an intricate writing. Below is just one of my favorites:<br/><br/><b>
  <i>"That cloak of love you were wearing—</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText10229043585426932063" style="display:none">5 STARS. <i>(EDIT: With more details)</i><br /><br />There are two kinds of a good book: those that you enjoy but will soon forget, and those that will linger in your memory forever. "The Storyteller" is the latter.<br /><br /><i>It's unlike anything you have ever read. Trust me.</i><br /><br />This book is brilliantly, beautifully written by Antonia Michaelis. I'm completely mesmerized by her words and her ability to interweave magic and realism in an intricate writing. Below is just one of my favorites:<br /><br /><b>
  <i>"That cloak of love you were wearing—he’s torn it to shreds, undoing the seams of trust that held it together. How can you ever wear those shreds?</i>
</b><br /><br />Isn't it beautiful? Hello, the Beauty of Literature. I'm inlove.<br /><br />The story, however, is painful, enchantingly dark, and depressing. Sounds like your not kind of book? Not my kind either. It's like I have a love-hate relationship with this book. The turn of events are truly devastating, Anna is as stubborn as she is soft-hearted, and Abel is.. well, he's entirely different from the person I thought he was. But oh God, <b>no one can ignore the brilliance of this book.</b> The author is a genius for writing TWO STORIES at the same time, paralleling them perfectly. Here's an example:<br /><br />Abel telling a story to Micha (his sister) and Anna - <b>
  <i>"Come on, you must be hungry," a rose girl said, and the rose people led the little queen farther inland, till they reached a small pavilion filled with rosebushes. </i>
</b><br /><br />That was a few days after they met Anna. Clearly, she's the Rose Girl in Abel's fairytale. Everything and everyone in his story matches up the reality with a hint of mystery. And it doesn't stop there, it goes on and on and on as they meet new people and continue with their adventure. I'm completely in awe!<br /><br />It sort of reminds me of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15818969.The_Sea_of_Tranquility" title="The Sea of Tranquility by Katja Millay" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sea of Tranquility</a> because it's written so well and the unfolding of events is slow yet so spellbinding. The only difference is, this book is so much darker and the romance is different in so many ways. It will certainly open your eyes to <b>
  <i>truths that are no fairytale.</i>
</b><br /><br />Overall, this is magical realism at its finest. Truly <b>OUTSTANDING</b>!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10229043585426932063" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer903408683399156385">Oh! It hurts! =(<br/><br/>For the record, I would like to state- for obvious dark and disturbing reasons, that this is <i>not</i> a Tina book. <br/>But, I find myself in a very rare moment. I'd be lying if I said that I didn't recognize sensational writing, heart-aching characters and a powerful plot. <b>The storyteller</b> is a book I knew I shouldn't be reading, but the way it moves was so very enchanting that I couldn't stop myself even if I wanted too.<br/>I would have to agree with one of my GR friends, Rachel. This book re</span>
  <span id="freeText903408683399156385" style="display:none">Oh! It hurts! =(<br /><br />For the record, I would like to state- for obvious dark and disturbing reasons, that this is <i>not</i> a Tina book. <br />But, I find myself in a very rare moment. I'd be lying if I said that I didn't recognize sensational writing, heart-aching characters and a powerful plot. <b>The storyteller</b> is a book I knew I shouldn't be reading, but the way it moves was so very enchanting that I couldn't stop myself even if I wanted too.<br />I would have to agree with one of my GR friends, Rachel. This book really did just <i>destroy me</i>. It's beautiful and painful, heartwarming and heartbreaking, magical and raw. <br />It's the kind of story that will stay in my head for a long time to come but it's also an unforgettable tale that apart of me wishes I could forget.<br /></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_287615664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/287615664" />
    <a title="Parvathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy"><img alt="Parvathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1425840439p2/4915009.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/287615664?book_show_action=true">Mar 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Parvathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Parvathy" href="/user/show/4915009-parvathy">Parvathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Anyone who loves a good story</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Parvathy by: </span>
      goodreads
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=glued-till-the-last-page">glued-till-the-last-page</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=movie-material">movie-material</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=living-vicariously">living-vicariously</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4915009-parvathy?shelf=please-pass-the-tissues">please-pass-the-tissues</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer287615664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11884443227109348059"> <b>
  <i> A good girl.<br/> A bad boy.<br/> A fairy tale that's true.<br/> A truth that is no fairy tale.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Once in a while you come across a book that has a story to tell you, a story so alive that you feel you are living it with your every heart beat. A story where nothing else matter except the story itself. A story that stays with you every waking moment and makes you wish that it was just a story, You are not living it you are reading it, that makes a whole lot of difference. Why can't you come out the trance it</span>
  <span id="freeText11884443227109348059" style="display:none"> <b>
  <i> A good girl.<br> A bad boy.<br> A fairy tale that's true.<br> A truth that is no fairy tale.</i>
</b><br><br>Once in a while you come across a book that has a story to tell you, a story so alive that you feel you are living it with your every heart beat. A story where nothing else matter except the story itself. A story that stays with you every waking moment and makes you wish that it was just a story, You are not living it you are reading it, that makes a whole lot of difference. Why can't you come out the trance it created? Why can't it just tell you a story and leave it at that? Why follow you around refusing to release you from its grip? Will you ever come out from the world it has created? <br><br><b>THE STORYTELLER</b><br><br>The Storyteller is not an answering man. You can ask questions but don't expect answers because he weaves words to make a story but not answers. That's what Abel is, he is a storyteller who weaves magical tales for his little sister Micha. Not a polish drug dealer, not a thug but deep down a story teller. But no one knows this part of his tale, they see him for what he shows, an outcast in a military parka with a cigarette in his hands and an earphone in his ears that plays white noises to keep the world out. <br><br><b>THE ROSE GIRL</b><br><br>Living inside her very own bubble. In the house with blue lights and robin's, the rose girl Anna's life changes the moment she sets her eyes on a tiny worn out doll in the student's lounge. Who could it belong to? This tiny doll which she had the insane urge to protect. Could it belong to the polish drug dealer with icy blue eyes? The intimidating outcast who has a little sister to look after. Does she want to venture in to this world outside her bubble? A dark unknown world where Abel weaves his story. To the world of a story teller and his little orphaned queen. Was she suppose to be a part of their story? <br><br><b> THE LITTLE ORPHAN QUEEN </b><br><br>The little queen has lived on her tiny island of rocks and cliffs all her life. With her beautiful white mare, her a one room castle, her canopy bed and her pink jacket with artificial fur. She was happy and content. She had a diamond heart which shone as bright as the sun. In the stories that Abel created his little sister Micha was the queen, the queen with the diamond heart that others wanted. But the island was sinking and the queen had to reach the mainland before the man with the blond mustache claims her. The man who bears her name and will ask her to call him "father" when he meets her. He is not alone in his pursuits. There is the diamond trader who wants to take her away and trade her diamond heart. There is the diamond cutter who wants to cut out and shape her diamond heart to her liking. Can she out run them and reach the main land with the help of her sea lion protector, her rose girl and rest of her motley crew?. She has only has to hold on till her brother's 18th birthday to reach mainland.<br><br><b> BLOSSOMING LOVE </b><br><br>Why can't Anna leave the polish drug dealer alone? Why is she so determined to be a part of his story? Why is she following him around and listening to the stories he create? Is she willing to leave the island of roses to be a part of the little queen's crew? Because it is a journey that could never bring her back. <br><br>The sea lion never liked the island of roses. There was too many thorns and it was way different from their island. But the rose girl has found a place in their journey. She protected the little queen and in the process gave her heart to the story teller. Everything was the same in the island of roses. She was waiting for the little queen. But the story teller was wary, the rose girl did not belong here. She has a different path ahead of her. One with less perils and a happy ending. Why does she want to be a part of something so disastrous that even the story teller cannot predict the outcome. <br><br><b> THE ISLAND OF MURDERERS </b><br><br>The island of murderers is empty. Which means the murderer was with them all along. The one who was killing off the villains in the story and in real life, starting with the man with the blond mustache, Micha's father and then the diamond trader, the social services agent. Is the murderer really among them ? Is it the sea lion which can turn in to a giant wolf when the occasion calls for it? How far will the he go to protect his queen? Did the rose girl really fall in love with a murderer? The story teller who can weave magic with words, the one who has hurt her and gave her a scar which would never fade. Is he capable of murder? If so will their journey have a happy ending or will the selfless rose girl fade away like all the other characters in his story?<br><br>A single red rose in a sea of eternal winter. Will summer come for them? These broken characters trying to reach the mainland. Only time will tell. A story can be told in so many different ways but only a true storyteller can tell you a story in a way that touches your heart and leave a lasting impression. Antonia Michaelis is one such story teller and this story a single red rose. Tears are rolling down my cheeks while I say goodbye to them. Those wonderful characters that has enchanted me. Maybe I don't have to say goodbye after all, I could make up my very own story for them. If there is one thing that this book teaches you, then it is the power of a good story to captivate you. <br><br>I was in double mind about reading this book. After reading the synopsis it is very difficult to comprehend that there is going to be a happy ending coming your way and I am not a fan of sad endings. But curiously most sad ending books end up as my favorite. Antonia Michaelis "The Story Teller" is a different kind of an experience. Is there a novelty in the story?. At first glance the answer is no. There are a lot of stories out there with a tortured hero with responsibilities and a kindhearted girl who wants to show him some happiness in life. In the end either everything turns out happy or sad. But does it really make a difference? My answer would be no it is not the ending that makes the difference but the path that gets you there. If the path is contrived, boring and unrelated you would be happy that the characters had removed themselves from the face earth. The best decision they made in this whole story, by relieving the earth of their burden. But if the path is imaginative and wonderful, with moments that nurture your creativity and enlighten your mind then you end up with a different sort of nameless, confused emotion that leaves you fulfilled and incomplete at the same time. That leaves a whole in your heart that your never want to fill up and this quality is the novelty in this story. The in depth emotions, the strained relationships, the threatening secrets and a fairy tale that binds them all together. A fairy tale whose landscapes arise out of their doubts, the islands symbolic of their points in life and a path as treacherous as the frozen ocean in winter that can give away any time.<br><br>A story within a story but which do you prefer? Antonia's or Abel's. At times I thought Abel's was a distraction from the true story line but as the story progressed I began to realize that the story is not just a story but an insight in to the mind of a simple story teller. A mind so full of emotions that a simple rambling in between lines is not enough to bring out his true self but a beautiful story told in the simplest of words. A story where every one was trying to save the little queen. But was it the queen that needed the saving. Is she the victim here or is the subtlest of hints pointing to a different character altogether. The rose girl Anna, the one who wants to come out of her bubble only to realize that she was the only one without it in the first place. Everyone around her has created a small bubble around themselves which she mistook for her own. She saw what others couldn't see but was her sight a gift or a burden. After finishing this story I am still trying to find the answers to these questions but in this story there are no straight answers only more question because in this world there are more questions than answers. Sometimes even the right question has no answers. A truly imaginative and wonderful book that will leave you shattered in such a way that even if you pick up the pieces and arrange them in order you could never be the same. A must read.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371347i/724381._SX540_.jpg" width="200" height="200" alt="Snow Rose" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="11884443227109348059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_579602723" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/579602723" />
    <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse"><img alt="Ms. Smartarse" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1401273675p2/13703358.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/579602723?book_show_action=true">Apr 03, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ms. Smartarse" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ms. Smartarse" href="/user/show/13703358-ms-smartarse">Ms. Smartarse</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9783789142895" href="/book/show/9969688-der-m-rchenerz-hler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=murder">murder</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=cover-love">cover-love</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13703358-ms-smartarse?shelf=drama">drama</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer579602723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1662280206156014641"><em>Translated into English, as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11284898-the-storyteller' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Storyteller</a> (see <a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0oPa0Fd1zfg' rel='nofollow noopener'>the English trailer</a>).</em><br/><br/>Anna is a good kid, on the brink of her final high school exams. She's determined to do well, take a year off, and eventually leave the "soap bubble" she's been living in. But she finds herself increasingly distracted by the mysterious Abel, one of her bad boy classmates, rumored to be a drug dealer.<br/><br/>Hit with a strong stalkerish urge, Anna starts following him around, and soon finds out that Abel has a 6 year-old sister, to who</span>
  <span id="freeText1662280206156014641" style="display:none"><em>Translated into English, as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11284898-the-storyteller" rel="nofollow noopener">The Storyteller</a> (see <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0oPa0Fd1zfg" rel="nofollow noopener">the English trailer</a>).</em><br><br>Anna is a good kid, on the brink of her final high school exams. She's determined to do well, take a year off, and eventually leave the "soap bubble" she's been living in. But she finds herself increasingly distracted by the mysterious Abel, one of her bad boy classmates, rumored to be a drug dealer.<br><br>Hit with a strong stalkerish urge, Anna starts following him around, and soon finds out that Abel has a 6 year-old sister, to whom he's been telling a strange but eerily familiar fairy tale. As the story progresses, our characters grow closer, tragedy strikes, and the fairy tale that mirrors their lives much too closely starts to foreshadow a grim future.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1424003095i/13701920._SX540_.jpg" alt="Abel and Micha" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I had initially chosen <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9969688.Der_M_rchenerz_hler" title="Der Märchenerzähler by Antonia Michaelis" rel="nofollow noopener">The Storyteller</a>, based on its readability factor. Unlike the other German books I've tried reading before, I actually understood most of the first page in this one. Part of the YA genre, and chock full of raving ratings, I was fully prepared to be fairly underwhelmed, and yet... <br><br>It was Anna's "inner Gitta" that drew me in right from the start. I greatly enjoyed the motherly tone that the heroine would channel through Gitta, and then go ahead and ignore its sensible advice. I don't think I cared much about the "real" Gitta, but I really liked Anna's inner voice. After that, it was the fairy tale within the story that kept me reading. I definitely felt the same excitement that Micha did, whenever Abel would finally pick its narrative up.<br><br><strong>Score: 4/5 stars</strong><br><br>While, on the whole, I did get the symbolism of it all, I much preferred to 'listen' to the fairy tale as a stand-alone fantastic universe. Dreadfully superficial of me perhaps, but I ended up enjoying the story a lot more this way.<br><br>I found the ending appropriately tragic, though not irrevocably so... which is an interesting point in its favor. All in all: a good book, which managed to avoid getting not overly cheesy in style.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1662280206156014641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_285473086" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/285473086" />
    <a title="Wendy F" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4019599-wendy-f"><img alt="Wendy F" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1486662406p2/4019599.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/285473086?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy F" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy F" href="/user/show/4019599-wendy-f">Wendy F</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4019599-wendy-f?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer285473086" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14467087569503295565"><b>Update</b><br/>I can't get this book out of my head. I talk about it at random times and I think about it very often. I had to bump it up another star, because it obviously affected me deeply.<br/><br/><b>Original Review</b><br/>This book started out really strong. I immediately noticed how beautiful the prose was, especially for a translated book. I really liked the characters, and I loved the way that you got snapshot POV's for other side characters. Sometimes the characters did things that I didn't like, but every single t</span>
  <span id="freeText14467087569503295565" style="display:none"><b>Update</b><br />I can't get this book out of my head. I talk about it at random times and I think about it very often. I had to bump it up another star, because it obviously affected me deeply.<br /><br /><b>Original Review</b><br />This book started out really strong. I immediately noticed how beautiful the prose was, especially for a translated book. I really liked the characters, and I loved the way that you got snapshot POV's for other side characters. Sometimes the characters did things that I didn't like, but every single time I could understand what drove them to do the things they did. These were exceptionally flawed characters, especially Abel. <br /><br />I also loved, so much, the way the book read as though it was old fashioned. That beautiful prose almost left you with a sense of a historical, except you knew that it was modern times because of the phones they mentioned and references to the internet. I thought that added to the depth of the story. And this was one deep story.<br /><br />Anna notices the 'Polish peddler' one day at school and something happens that draw these two together. He's reluctant but she manages to worm her way into his heart, and boy did Abel love with a serious depth. Over the course of their book you get a very intricate fairy tale that Abel is telling Misha his little sister, and through the fairy tale you get a glimpse of the intricacies that make up Abel.<br /><br />(Don't read this unless you've finished the book!)<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I knew. The whole time I knew that it was Abel. It was a lot like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1162022.On_the_Jellicoe_Road" title="On the Jellicoe Road by Melina Marchetta" rel="nofollow noopener">Jellicoe Road</a>, people. It wasn't that you shouldn't know the secret, it was about the way the secret is revealed. That is the brilliance. And for the record, I never hated Abel. I still have no problem loving him. What he did was horrible, terrible. What was done TO HIM was horrible, terrible. Does that excuse him? No way. He knew that though. He didn't want to be excused or forgiven. What it does do is make it easy to sympathize. At least it did for me. I, like Anna, was able to still love him even if I couldn't forgive him. And that's about the rape and the murders. I mean, how many times does a man have to say 'stop, no'? In my opinion, Anna was also wrong, albeit on a smaller scale. I was uncomfortable with the scene long before he lost control because Abel kept saying he didn't want it. Just because a man has an erection does not mean he WANTS sex! It's a body's reaction to stimulation and they can't prevent it. Anna's not listening to him was also wrong, it doesn't matter that he was the man. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />I also really loved the ending. I was so sad, but I understood. On a less devastating level, it was what I hoped would happen.<br /><br />Now, I've gushed and gushed about this book, so your asking yourself why only 3 stars. I read the first half of this book rabidly. But at about 56% I sort of lost steam. It started becoming more of a chore. When I got to about 80% I got back into it, though. I'm not positive what happened in that 20% of the book, honestly. I think... I think maybe it just got so... sad, lol. I think it was hard to read for me because it was just so desolate. The whole tone of the book was down trodden and heartbreaking and I think it just got to me.<br /><br />I'll still recommend this book like crazy. Despite my 3 star rating, I absolutely still believe it deserves recognition. The End</span>
  <a data-text-id="14467087569503295565" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_280973240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/280973240" />
    <a title="Isamlq" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq"><img alt="Isamlq" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483590305p2/4016030.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/280973240?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Isamlq" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Isamlq" href="/user/show/4016030-isamlq">Isamlq</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781419700477" href="/book/show/10806009-the-storyteller">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4016030-isamlq?shelf=aaw-yeah">aaw-yeah</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer280973240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9818108557543093479">It’s one story in another with one mirroring the other. His story for his sister was magical and lovely. Only up close, it’s really quite a sad one because once you see who was who and what stood for what; then you could see/feel just how far removed his stories were from their reality. And their reality? Stark, depressing, and so far from even the possibility of a happily-ever-after. <br/><br/>If at first, like Anna, I was drawn to him, impressed by him and maybe, just, maybe slightly in love with his po</span>
  <span id="freeText9818108557543093479" style="display:none">It’s one story in another with one mirroring the other. His story for his sister was magical and lovely. Only up close, it’s really quite a sad one because once you see who was who and what stood for what; then you could see/feel just how far removed his stories were from their reality. And their reality? Stark, depressing, and so far from even the possibility of a happily-ever-after. <br /><br />If at first, like Anna, I was drawn to him, impressed by him and maybe, just, maybe slightly in love with his possibilities; those sudden turn of events had me not just pausing, but recoiling from him. From totally loving him, rooting for him and damning everyone else that said otherwise… that moment had me stopping in my tracks. It had me so angry <i>at </i>him, but more, it had me heartbroken <i>for</i> her. I confess I put it down with no intention of picking it up back again. But it kept nagging at me: how would the author pick up the pieces; where would the story go? <br /><br />Setting aside the device of a story in another one, the mystery aspect only took precedence once I was less in love with the idea of them together. They all had me wondering. Was what I was thinking right? Was I wrong in how I’d first pegged them at first? That heartbreaking, devastating twist seemed to be pointing to the affirmative. <b>Here’s the truth:</b> The clues left here and there had me feeling secure in the knowledge that I knew who the baddy was. <b>And here’s another truth: </b> <i>I was wrong </i> to an extent.<br /> <br />With the mystery slow to pick up, I was half tempted to skim over his stories. I knew something similar to what he was saying would be laid out sooner or later in a clearer, more contemporary voice. I’m glad I didn’t because contrasting his fairytale against their reality, things balanced out a little. His stories calmed things down I suppose. <br /><br />Not since Tabitha Suzuma’s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7600924-forbidden" rel="nofollow noopener">Forbidden</a> have feelings of such conflict in me been roused. And as far as story devices go, his fairytale foreshadowing everything else was different… new… special. And it was what had Abel as Storyteller winding around me. Such a good brother, such a good man, he had me feeling all hopeful. Again that one moment put a stop to those feelings. After that all there was pity, anger, disappointment. But wait a couple of beats, and it was her turn to have me more than slightly confused. Her choices, her decisions astonished me. Truly, the one thing I cannot move on from is the absence of a resolution for her. I mean she was all, <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>"Let's not forgive and let's not forget."</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> But, I was all, "<b>
  <i>How is that even possible?!" </i>
</b> <br /><br />The Storyteller went from sweet to devastating to totally unexpected then heartbreaking again. <br /><br /><b>3.5/5</b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9818108557543093479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_310478721" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/310478721" />
    <a title="Susana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7301000-susana"><img alt="Susana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1483821488p2/7301000.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/310478721?book_show_action=true">Apr 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Susana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Susana" href="/user/show/7301000-susana">Susana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=magical-realism">magical-realism</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=hell-no">hell-no</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=go-away-and-never-come-back">go-away-and-never-come-back</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7301000-susana?shelf=heartbreaking-stories">heartbreaking-stories</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer310478721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8319071185920323880">Honestly i don't know quite what to write about this story...<br/>I don't even know what rating i should give it.<br/><br/>For most part of the book, i HATED the story. And i couldn't connect with one of the characters.<br/><br/>This is probably the most difficult book that i ever had to read in a long, long time. <br/>When i started it, i was expecting drama, but not THIS.<br/><br/> This is one of those books that are meant to break one's hearts. This was so painful, so sad, so hopeless, so lost....that i don't even know what to thin</span>
  <span id="freeText8319071185920323880" style="display:none">Honestly i don't know quite what to write about this story...<br />I don't even know what rating i should give it.<br /><br />For most part of the book, i HATED the story. And i couldn't connect with one of the characters.<br /><br />This is probably the most difficult book that i ever had to read in a long, long time. <br />When i started it, i was expecting drama, but not THIS.<br /><br /> This is one of those books that are meant to break one's hearts. This was so painful, so sad, so hopeless, so lost....that i don't even know what to think about it. <br /><br />For one side this could be seen as an amazing piece of work... But on another one, i have to say that i've never read anything so twisted and at times ridiculous. There's no fucking excuse (sorry my language!) for RAPE!! NONE!!!!! And to imagine an adolescent reading this and trying to find a comparison to something that may have happened to her/him, and coming to the conclusion that there is an excuse....WELL, I DON'T LIKE THAT. For me, the author killed the book with the rape scene and with Anna forgiving him. You can't write things like that.<br /><br />'The storyteller' is like a trap that caughts you and binds you _ kicking and screaming _ until you finish it. Even when i was hating what i was reading, i had to know how this one was going to end.<br /><br /> Reading this at times, was like seing a portuguese movie _ yes, i'm portuguese so i know first hand of what i'm talking about _ the strangeness, the weirdness, the sense of disaster looming on the horizon, it was all there! And since i HATE that kind of movies, guess what i was feeling while reading this story...<br /><br />The writing. At the beginning, i had a really hard time with it, but then the THING grew on me, like a flower, who at the beginning looks suspiciouly like a weed.<br /><br />The characters, well i really wanted to scream at the author at times. I wanted to say: I KNOW THIS IS NOT A FAIRY TALE; BUT ENOUGH IS ENOUGH!! Why did that scene had to be writen? Abel could have just left...because with that scene, it was over for me.<br /><br /><br />This book is about a storyteller, Abel, who will do anything to protect his little sister. Abel who was an abused child, a neglected child, who grow up into a teenager capable of doing anything in his power to make sure that had happened to him, would never happen to his sister.<br /><br />One of better aspects of this story, are indeed the stories that Abel makes up for his sister. In them, their life is portrayed as a fantastic quest, in which the little Queen _ Abel's sister _ will try to reach a new home. Through many dangers, and with the help of some loyal friends, the little Queen journey is heartbreaking in her representation of the life that brother and sister have.<br /><br />And then there's Anna. I didn't like this representation of a seventeen year old girl. Better yet the representation of a protected seventeen year old girl, who decides on a WHIM _ what other word can i use? _ to change her way of being....who gets obsessed over a boy because of a single conversation with him, just felt too cliché and improbable for me. <br /><br />All of a sudden the good girl, whom is called by her best friend as "little lamb", who never noticed the "bad" boy that sells drugs on school decides to start following him around. A boy she had never payed attention too. By Anna's own words: "...was it white in summer, too? She couldn't remember. She hadn't looked at him once last summer. He'd been there at school, but not existing."<br /><br />Oh, he existed...people don't stop existing simply because others pay no attention to them.<br /><br />All of a sudden the girl who always lived in a beautiful bubble, filled with blue light _ the character has a thing with this... _ decides that she wants to be around Abel and his sister. The girl that talks to her parents by their given names, and who doesn't give them any kind of satisfaction. Apparently things in German are really modern..<br /><br />If you start this one, don't expect a story about salvation. This one's about the never ending nighmare of some people's life's. Honestly i don't recommend this to anyone.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8319071185920323880" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
